## The Three Approaches

### Approach 1: Pure Signal Context (Kubernetes)

**Key File**: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/signal.go`

**Pattern**:
```go
ctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(context.Background())
signal.Notify(shutdownHandler, SIGTERM, SIGINT)
go func() {
    <-shutdownHandler      // First signal
    cancel()               // Cancel context
    <-shutdownHandler      // Second signal
    os.Exit(1)            // Immediate exit
}()
```

**Characteristics**:
- Simple and reusable
- Immediate cancellation on first signal
- Force exit on second signal
- All components use context.Done()

**Best for**: Simple architectures, microservices

### Approach 2: Signal + Timeout (Grafana)

**Key File**: `pkg/cmd/grafana-server/commands/cli.go`

**Pattern**:
```go
signal.Notify(sigChan, SIGINT, SIGTERM)
ctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(ctx, 30*time.Second)
s.Shutdown(ctx, reason)  // Bounded shutdown time
```

**Characteristics**:
- Separate SIGHUP (reload) and SIGTERM (shutdown)
- Explicit timeout (30 seconds)
- sync.Once prevents multiple shutdowns
- Coordinated component shutdown

**Best for**: Complex systems with multiple services

### Approach 3: Component Registry (Prometheus)

**Key File**: `cmd/prometheus/main.go` using `oklog/run`

**Pattern**:
```go
var g run.Group
g.Add(signalHandler_runFunc, signalHandler_stopFunc)
g.Add(component1_runFunc, component1_stopFunc)
g.Add(component2_runFunc, component2_stopFunc)
g.Run()  // First component exit triggers cascade
```

**Characteristics**:
- Explicit shutdown ordering
- Each component has run/stop functions
- Cascading shutdown via oklog/run
- Guarantees order: discovery -> scraper -> TSDB

**Best for**: Highly coupled components with critical ordering

---

## Critical Pattern: Cleanup Ordering

All three repositories enforce a strict cleanup order:

1. **Stop accepting new work**
   - Disable health checks
   - Close listening ports
   - Mark as unhealthy

2. **Drain in-flight operations**
   - Complete current requests
   - Process pending notifications
   - Flush buffers

3. **Stop background goroutines**
   - Cancel context propagation
   - Signal workers to stop
   - Wait for completion

4. **Close resources**
   - Close databases
   - Close network connections
   - Release file handles

**Why this order matters**:
- Prevents lost requests
- Ensures data consistency
- Avoids deadlocks
- Allows graceful degradation

---

## Implementation Checklist

When implementing graceful shutdown:

- [ ] Register signal handler for SIGTERM and SIGINT
- [ ] Create context for cancellation propagation
- [ ] Implement shutdown timeout (recommended 30s)
- [ ] Guard shutdown with sync.Once
- [ ] Define component stop order
- [ ] Drain in-flight requests
- [ ] Log shutdown events
- [ ] Test double signal (force exit)
- [ ] Test timeout scenario
- [ ] Verify no data loss

## Common Code Patterns

### Pattern 1: Basic Signal Handler
```go
sigChan := make(chan os.Signal, 1)
signal.Notify(sigChan, syscall.SIGINT, syscall.SIGTERM)
<-sigChan  // Block until signal
// Shutdown code
```

### Pattern 2: Context Cancellation
```go
ctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(context.Background())
go func() {
    <-sigChan
    cancel()
}()
// Pass ctx to components
```

### Pattern 3: Timeout Enforcement
```go
ctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(ctx, 30*time.Second)
defer cancel()
err := server.Shutdown(ctx)
if err == context.DeadlineExceeded {
    // Timeout occurred
}
```

### Pattern 4: Single Execution Guard
```go
shutdownOnce sync.Once
shutdownOnce.Do(func() {
    // Shutdown code
    // Runs only once
})
```

### Pattern 5: Component Registry
```go
var g run.Group
g.Add(run, stop)  // Each component
g.Run()           // Orchestrated execution
```

---

## Timeout Strategies

| Repository | Timeout | Strategy | Use Case |
|------------|---------|----------|----------|
| Kubernetes | None | Immediate context cancel | Simple services |
| Grafana | 30s | Explicit WithTimeout | Complex systems |
| Prometheus | Dynamic | Per-component draining | Tight coupling |

## Conclusion

Graceful shutdown is a critical aspect of production Go services. The three approaches found in these repositories represent the spectrum from simple to complex:

- **Kubernetes**: Simplicity and reusability
- **Grafana**: Bounded shutdown with multiple components
- **Prometheus**: Explicit ordering for critical dependencies

The key principles common to all three are:

1. Signal handler registration
2. Context-based propagation
3. Timeout enforcement
4. Cleanup ordering
5. Proper synchronization

Choose the approach that fits your architecture and always remember: **the order of shutdown matters**.
